[^1093]: From Yasna X, 20 (62), where, instead of the words, 'in the ox is our strength (amem), in the ox is our need,' the text has, 'in the ox is his need, in the ox is our need,' meaning, 'when we give him his need (water and grass), he gives us our need (milk and calves),' (Pahl. tr.).

[^1094]: See [p. 120](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2315.htm#page_120), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2315.htm#fn_558).

[^1095]: Who shall offer a sacrifice to Verethraghna.

* * *

[pg 249]

## XV. RĀM YAŚT.


_May Ahura Mazda be rejoiced! . . . ._ {#XV:0}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_I confess myself a worshipper of Mazda, a follower of Zarathuśtra, one who hates the Daēvas, and obeys the laws of Ahura;_

_For sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification unto \[Hāvani\], the holy and master of holiness . . . ._

Unto Rāma Hvāstra, unto Vayu who works highly and is more powerful to afflict than all other creatures [^1096],

_Be propitiation from me, for sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification._

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

#### I.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them [^1097]. I will sacrifice to Peace, whose breath is friendly, and to Weal, both of them. {#XV:1}

[pg 250]

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke, for this house, for the master of this house, and for the man here who is offering libations and giving gifts. To this excellent God do we sacrifice, that he may accept our meat and our prayers, and grant us in return to crush our enemies at one stroke.

 [^1098]. To him did the Maker, Ahura Mazda, offer up a sacrifice in the Airyana Vaējah 1, on a golden throne, under golden beams [^1099] and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\] [^1100]. {#XV:2}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly [^1101], that I may smite the creation of Angra Mainyu, and that nobody may smite this creation of the Good Spirit!' {#XV:3}

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:4}

We sacrifice to the holy Vayu: we sacrifice to Vayu, who works highly. {#XV:5}

To this part of thee do we sacrifice, O Vayu! that belongs to Speṇta Mainyu [^1102].

For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard, namely, unto the awful Vayu, who works highly. We offer up a sacrifice unto the awful Vayu, who works highly, with the libations, with the Haoma and meat, with the baresma, with the wisdom of the tongue, with the [pg 251] holy spells, the words, the deeds, the libations, and the well-spoken words.

_Yēṇhē hātãm: All those beings of whom Ahura Mazda . . . ._

#### II.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:6}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . . [^1103]

To him did Haoshyangha, the Paradhāta, offer up a sacrifice on the Taēra of the Hara, bound with iron [^1104], on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offering of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:7}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may smite two-thirds of the Daēvas of Māzana and of the fiends of Varena [^1105].' {#XV:8}

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda [^1106], did pursue it. {#XV:9}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### III.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:10}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

[pg 252]

To him did Takhma Urupa [^1107], the well-armed [^1108], offer up a sacrifice on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:11}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may conquer all Daēvas and men, all the Yātus and Pairikas, and that I may ride Angra Mainyu, turned into the shape of a horse, all around the earth from one end to the other, for thirty years.' {#XV:12}

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon [^1109], as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:13}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### IV.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:14}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

Unto him did the bright Yima, the good shepherd, [pg 253] sacrifice from the height Hukairya, the all-shining and golden, on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:15}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may become the most glorious of the men born to behold the sun: that I may make in my reign both animals and men undying, waters and plants undrying, and the food for eating creatures never-failing [^1110].' {#XV:16}

In the reign of the valiant Yima there was neither cold wind nor hot wind, neither old age nor death, nor envy made by the Daēvas [^1111].

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:17}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### V.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:18}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

Unto him did the three-mouthed Aži Dahāka offer up a sacrifice in his accursed palace of Kviriṇta [^1112], [pg 254] on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:19}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may make all the seven Karshvares of the earth empty of men [^1113].' {#XV:20}

In vain did he sacrifice, in vain did he beg, in vain did he invoke, in vain did he give gifts, in vain did he bring libations; Vayu did not grant him that boon. {#XV:21}

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### VI.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:22}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

Unto him did Thraētaona, the heir of the valiant Āthwya clan, offer up a sacrifice in the four-cornered Varena, on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:23}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may overcome Aži Dahāka, the three-mouthed, the three-headed, the six-eyed, who has a thousand senses, that most powerful, fiendish Druj, that [pg 255] demon baleful to the world, the strongest Drum that Angra Mainyu created against the material world, to destroy the world of the good principle; and that I may deliver his two wives, Savanghavāc and Erenavāc, who are the fairest of body amongst women, and the most wonderful creatures in the world [^1114].' {#XV:24}

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:25}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### VII.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:26}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

To him did the manly-hearted Keresāspa [^1115] offer up a sacrifice by the Gudha [^1116], a channel of the Rangha, made by Mazda, upon a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:27}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may succeed in avenging my brother Urvākhshaya [^1117], that I may smite Hitāspa and yoke him to my chariot.' {#XV:28}

The Gaṇdarewa, who lives beneath the waters, [pg 256] is the son of Ahura in the deep, he is the only master of the deep [^1118].

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:29}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### VIII.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:30}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

To him did Aurvasāra [^1119], the lord of the country, offer up a sacrifice, towards the White Forest [^1120], by the White Forest, on the border of the White Forest, on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of full-boiling \[milk\]. {#XV:31}

He begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that the gallant Husravah, he who unites the Aryan nations into one kingdom [^1121], may not smite us; that I may flee from king Husravah [^1122]; . . . . {#XV:32}

[pg 257]

'That king Husravah and all the Aryans in the Forest may smite him [^1123].'

Vayu, who works highly, granted him that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:33}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### IX.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:34}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

To him did Hutaosa, she of the many brothers [^1124], of the Naotara house [^1125], offer up a sacrifice, on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of boiling milk. {#XV:35}

She begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant me this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that I may be dear and loved and well-received in the house of king Vīśtāspa.' {#XV:36}

Vayu, who works highly, granted her that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:37}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### X.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:38}

[pg 258]

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

To him did [^1126] the maids, whom no man had known, offer up a sacrifice on a golden throne, under golden beams and a golden canopy, with bundles of baresma and offerings of boiling milk. {#XV:39}

They begged of him a boon, saying: 'Grant us this, O Vayu! who dost work highly, that we may find a husband, young and beautiful of body, who will treat us well, all life long, and give us offspring; a wise, learned, ready-tongued husband.' {#XV:40}

Vayu, who works highly, granted them that boon, as the Maker, Ahura Mazda, did pursue it. {#XV:41}

_We sacrifice to the holy Vayu . . . ._

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### XI.

I will sacrifice to the Waters and to Him who divides them . . . . {#XV:42}

To this Vayu do we sacrifice, this Vayu do we invoke . . . .

We sacrifice to that Vayu that belongs to the Good Spirit [^1127], the bright and glorious Vayu.

My name is Vayu, O holy Zarathuśtra! My name is Vayu, because I go through (vyēmi) the two worlds [^1128], the one which the Good Spirit has [pg 259] made and the one which the Evil Spirit has made. {#XV:43}

My name is the Overtaker (apaēta), O holy Zarathuśtra! My name is the Overtaker, because I can overtake the creatures of both worlds, the one that the Good Spirit has made and the one that the Evil Spirit has made.

My name is the All-smiting, O holy Zarathuśtra! My name is the All-smiting, because I can smite the creatures of both worlds, the one that the Good Spirit has made and the one that the Evil Spirit has made. {#XV:44}

My name is the Worker of Good, O holy Zarathuśtra! My name is the Worker of Good, because I work the good of the Maker, Ahura Mazda, and of the Amesha-Speṇtas [^1129].

My name is He that goes forwards. {#XV:45}

My name is He that goes backwards.

My name is He that bends backwards.

My name is He that hurls away.

My name is He that hurls down.

My name is He that destroys.

My name is He that takes away.

My name is He that finds out.

My name is He that finds out the Glory (Hvarenō).

My name is the Valiant; my name is the Most Valiant. {#XV:46}

My name is the Strong; my name is the Strongest.

My name is the Firm; my name is the Firmest.

My name is the Stout; my name is the Stoutest.

My name is He that crosses over easily.

My name is He that goes along hurling away.

[pg 260]

My name is He that crushes at one stroke.

My name is . . . . [^1130]

My name is He that works against the Daēvas.

My name is . . . . [^1131]

My name is He that prevails over malice; my name is He that destroys malice. {#XV:47}

My name is He that unites; my name is He that re-unites; my name is He that separates.

My name is the Burning; my name is the Quick of intelligence [^1132].

My name is Deliverance; my name is Welfare [^1133].

My name is the Burrows; my name is He who destroys the burrows [^1134]; my name is He who spits upon the burrows [^1135].

My name is Sharpness of spear; my name is He of the sharp spear. {#XV:48}

My name is Length of spear; my name is He of the long spear.

My name is Piercingness of spear; my name is He of the piercing spear.

My name is the Glorious; my name is the Over-glorious.

Invoke these names of mine, O holy Zarathuśtra! in the midst of the havocking hordes, in the midst of the columns moving forwards, in the strife of the conflicting nations. {#XV:496}

[pg 261]

Invoke these names of mine, O holy Zarathuśtra! when the all-powerful tyrant of a country falls upon thee, rushes upon thee, deals wounds upon thee, or hurls his chariot against thee, to rob thee [^1136] of thy wealth, to rob thee of thy health. {#XV:50}

Invoke these names of mine, O holy Zarathuśtra! when the unholy Ashemaogha falls upon thee, rushes upon thee, deals wounds upon thee, or hurls his chariot against thee, to rob thee of thy strength, to rob thee of thy wealth, to rob thee of thy health. {#XV:51}

Invoke these names of mine, O holy Zarathuśtra! when a man stands in bonds, when a man is being thrown into bonds, or when a man is being dragged in bonds: thus the prisoners flee from the hands of those who carry them, they flee away out of the prison [^1137]. {#XV:52}

O thou Vayu! who strikest fear upon all men and horses, who in all creatures workest against the Daēvas, both into the lowest places and into those a thousand times deep dost thou enter with equal power [^1138]. {#XV:53}

'With what manner of sacrifice shall I worship thee? With what manner of sacrifice shall I forward and worship thee? With what manner of sacrifice will be achieved thy adoration, O great Vayu! thou who art high-up girded, firm, swift-moving, high-footed, wide-breasted, wide-thighed, with untrembling eyes, as powerful in sovereignty as any absolute sovereign in the world?' [pg 262] 55\. 'Take thou a baresma, O holy Zarathuśtra! turn it upwards or downwards, according as it is full day or dawning; upwards during the day, downwards at the dawn [^1139]. {#XV:54}

'If thou makest me worshipped with a sacrifice, then I shall say unto thee with my own voice things of health, made by Mazda and full of glory, so that Angra Mainyu may never do harm unto thee, nor the Yātus, nor those addicted to the works of the Yātu, whether Daēvas or men.' {#XV:56}

We sacrifice unto thee, O great Vayu! we sacrifice unto thee, O strong Vayu! {#XV:57}

We sacrifice unto Vayu, the greatest of the great;

we sacrifice unto Vayu, the strongest of the strong.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden helm.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden crown.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden necklace.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden chariot.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden wheel.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden weapons.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden garment.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden shoe.

We sacrifice unto Vayu, of the golden girdle.

We sacrifice unto the holy Vayu; we sacrifice unto Vayu, who works highly.

To this part of thee do we sacrifice, O Vayu! that belongs to the Good Spirit.

_For his brightness and glory, I will offer unto him a sacrifice worth being heard, namely, unto the awful Vayu, who works highly . . . ._

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._ {#XV:58}

I bless the sacrifice and invocation unto, and the [pg 263] strength and vigour of Rāma Hvāstra, and Vayu, who works highly, more powerful to afflict than all the other creatures: this part of thee that belongs to the Good Spirit.

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_\[Give\] unto that man brightness and glory, . . . . give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones._

[^1096]: Cf. Sīrōzah I, 22.

[^1097]: Apãm Napāṭ (Yt. VIII, 34) or Tiśtrya (Yt. VIII, 1).

[^1098]: Cf. Yt. V, 17.

[^1099]: Fraspāṭ, Persian ![](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/img/25000.jpg).

[^1100]: Cf. [p. 169](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2317.htm#page_169), note [5](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2317.htm#fn_783).

[^1101]: See [p. 10](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#page_10), note [4](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#fn_69).

[^1102]: As Vayu, the atmosphere, is the place in which the conflict of the two principles takes place, one part of him belongs to the Evil Spirit (see Vend. Introd. IV, 17).

[^1103]: The rest as in clause 1.

[^1104]: Cf. Yt. V, 21, [p. 58](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#page_58), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#fn_295).

[^1105]: Cf. Yt. V, 21-23.

[^1106]: Introduced from § 4 into this and all similar clauses, except the one relating to Aži Dahāka (§ 21).

[^1107]: Takhma Urupa (in later legend Tahmūrāf) was a brother to Yima. He reigned for thirty years and rode Ahriman, turned into a horse. But at last his wife, deceived by Ahriman, revealed to him the secret of her husband's power, and Tahmūrāf was swallowed up by his horse. But Yima managed to take back his brother's body from the body of Ahriman and recovered thereby the arts and civilisation which had disappeared along with Tahmūrāf (see Minokhired XXVII, 32; Ravāet apud Spiegel, Einleitung in die traditionelle Literatur, pp. 317 seq.; Ormazd et Ahriman, § 137 seq.; cf. above, [p. 60](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#page_60), note [1](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#fn_302)).

[^1108]: Azinavaṇṭ or zaēnahvaṇṭ: he kept that epithet in later tradition: Zīnavend, 'quod cognomen virum significat armis probe instructum' (Hamza Ispahensis, p. 20, tr. Gottwaldt).

[^1109]: As told Yt. XIX, 29.

[^1110]: Cf. Yasna IX, 4-5 (11-20) and Yt. XIX, 31 seq.

[^1111]: This passage is interpolated from Yasna IX, 5 (17-10.

[^1112]: Or, 'his accursed palace of the Stork' (upa kviriṇtem duzitem). 'Aži Dahāka,' says Hamza (p. 32 in the text, p. 22 in the translation), 'used to live in Babylon (cf. Yt. V, 29), where he had built a palace in the form of a stork; he called it Kuleng Dīs ( ![](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/img/25300.jpg)), the fortress of the Stork; the inhabitants called it Dis Het ( ![](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/img/25301.jpg)).' Kuleng Dīs was in Zend Kviriṇta daēza and Dis Het is nothing else than Dužita. One may doubt [pg 254] whether Kviriṇta is the name of a place or the Zend form of Kuleng, a stork: in any case it was a palace in Bawri (Babylon). In the Shah Nāmah it is called Dižukht (duž-ukhta for duž-ita; see Études Iraniennes, II, 211).

[^1113]: Cf. Yt. V, 30 seq.

[^1114]: Yt. V, 34; IX, 14; XVII, 34.

[^1115]: Cf. Yt. V, 37 seq.

[^1116]: An unknown affluent of the Rangha (Tigris).

[^1117]: Sāma had two sons, Keresāspa, a warrior, and Urvākhshaya, a judge and law-giver (Yasna IX, 10 \[29 seq.\]). We have no further details about Urvākhshaya's legend than that he was killed by 'Hitāspa, the golden-crowned' (cf. Yt. XIX, 4I), and avenged by Keresāspa.

[^1118]: A disconnected allusion to the struggle of Keresāspa with the Gaṇdarewa (Yt. V, 38, text and notes; XIX, 41). On the words 'the son of Ahura . . . .' cf. Ormazd et Ahriman, p. 215, note 1.

[^1119]: No other mention is made of Aurvasāra in the Avesta, unless he is alluded to in Yt. V, 50. He does not appear to have been. known to Firdausi.

[^1120]: Spaētiniś razūra is called 'the chief of forests' (Bund. XXIV, 16). According to the Bahman Yaśt (III, 9), it was the seat of the last and decisive battle between Arjāsp and Gūśtāsp.

[^1121]: Cf. Yt. V, 49; IX, 21.

[^1122]: Cf. Yt. V, 50.

[^1123]: This line looks as if it should belong to a counter-prayer by Husravah, which was heard by Vayu, as appears from Yt. V, 50.

[^1124]: See Yt. IX, 26.

[^1125]: See [p. 77](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#page_77), note [1](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#fn_381).

[^1126]: It may be doubted whether the allusion here is to a legend of marriage en masse, following the marriage of Hutaosa with Vīśtāspa, or whether the aorist is used with an indicative meaning: 'To him do the maids who have known no man . . . . They beg of him a boon, saying . . . .' Cf. Yt. XVI, 17.

[^1127]: Cf. § 5, note 5.

[^1128]: An attempt to an etymological explanation of the name Vayu. Cf. § 53.

[^1129]: He is their agent and instrument.

[^1130]: Āiniva (?).

[^1131]: Keredhariśa (?).

[^1132]: Doubtful; baoca, cf. ![](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/img/26000.jpg).

[^1133]: Reading sudhiś.

[^1134]: Geredha is the burrow of an Ahrimanian creature (see Vend. III, to \[33\]; VII, 24 \[60: Vayu, in that half of him that belongs to the Evil Spirit, is the seat (the burrow) of Ahriman; but with his better half, he struggles against the fiend and destroys him.

[^1135]: Cf. Yt. I, 11, 16.

[^1136]: Literally, coveting.

[^1137]: The translation of this clause is doubtful; the text is corrupt.

[^1138]: Cf. § 42.

[^1139]: Études Iraniennes, II, 110.

* * *

[pg 264]

## XVI. DĪN YAŚT.


_May Ahura Mazda be rejoiced! . . . ._ {#XVI:0}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_I confess myself a worshipper of Mazda, a follower of Zarathuśtra, one who hates the Daēvas and obeys the laws of Ahura;_

_For sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification unto \[Hāvani\], the holy and master of holiness . . . ._

To the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, and to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda,

Be propitiation from me, for sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification.

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

#### I.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda, the supplier of good [pg 265] stores, who runs quickly to the goal and frees one best from dangers [^1140], who brings libations, who is holy, clever, and renowned, speedy to work and quick of work; who goes quickly and cleanses well; the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda; {#XVI:1}

To whom Zarathuśtra did sacrifice, saying: 'Rise up from thy seat, come forward from the Abode [^1141], thou most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy. If thou art before me, stay for me; if thou art behind me, overtake me. {#XVI:2}

'Let everything be as friendly to us as anything can be: may we go smoothly along the roads, find good pathways in the mountains, run easily through the forests, and cross happily the rivers!' {#XVI:3}

For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard, namely, unto the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy. I will offer up a sacrifice unto the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, with the libations, with the Haoma and meat, with the baresma, with the wisdom of the tongue, with the holy spells, with the words and deeds, with the libations, with the well-spoken words. {#XVI:4}

_Yēṇhē hātãm: All those beings of whom Ahura Mazda . . . ._

#### II.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . [^1142] [pg 266] 6\. To whom Zarathuśtra did sacrifice for righteousness of thought, for righteousness of speech, for righteousness of deed, and for this boon, {#XVI:5}

That the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, would give him the swiftness of the feet, the quick hearing of the ears, the strength of the arms, the health of the whole body, the sturdiness of the whole body, and the eye-sight of the Kara fish, that lives beneath the waters, and can measure a rippling of the waters not thicker than a hair, in the Rangha, whose ends lie afar and whose depth is a thousand times the height of a man [^1143]. {#XVI:7}

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### III.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . {#XVI:8}

To whom Zarathuśtra did sacrifice for righteousness of thought, for righteousness of speech, for righteousness of deed, and for this boon, {#XVI:9}

That the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, would give him the swiftness of the feet, the quick hearing of the ears, the strength of the arms, the health of the whole body, the sturdiness of the whole body, and the eye-sight of the male horse, that, in the dark of the night, through the rain, the snow, the hail, or the sleet, from as far as nine districts, can perceive a horse's hair, mingled with the earth, and knows whether it is from the head or from the tail [^1144]. {#XVI:10}

[pg 267]

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### IV.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . {#XVI:11}

To whom Zarathuśtra did sacrifice for righteousness of thought, for righteousness of speech, for righteousness of deed, and for this boon, {#XVI:12}

That the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, would give him the swiftness of the feet, the quick hearing of the ears, the strength of the arms, the health of the whole body, the sturdiness of the whole body, and the eye-sight of the vulture with a golden collar, that, from as far as nine districts, can perceive a piece of flesh, not thicker than a fist, giving just as much light as a needle gives, as the point of a needle gives [^1145]. {#XVI:13}

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### V.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . {#XVI:14}

To whom the holy Hvōvi [^1146] did sacrifice with full knowledge, wishing that the holy Zarathuśtra would give her his good narcotic [^1147], that she might [pg 268] think according to the law, speak according to the law, and do according to the law. {#XVI:15}

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice, worth being heard . . . ._

#### VI.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . {#XVI:16}

To whom the Āthravans, sent afar [^1148], did sacrifice [^1149], wishing a good memory to preach the law, and wishing strength for their own body. {#XVI:17}

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

#### VII.

We sacrifice to the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy: we sacrifice to the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda . . . . {#XVI:18}

To whom the king of the country, the lord of the country does sacrifice, wishing peace for his country, wishing strength for his own body. {#XVI:19}

_For her brightness and glory, I will offer unto her a sacrifice worth being heard . . . ._

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._ {#XVI:20}

I bless the sacrifice and prayer, and the strength [pg 269] and vigour of the most right Cista, made by Mazda and holy, and of the good Law of the worshippers of Mazda.

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_\[Give\] unto that man brightness and glory, . . . . give him long, long life, give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones._

[^1140]: Reading nimareziśta; cf. vīmareziśtem, Yt. I, 2.

[^1141]: The heavenly abode, the Garōthmān.

[^1142]: The rest as in § 1.

[^1143]: Cf. Yt. XIV, 29.

[^1144]: Cf. Yt. XIV, 31.

[^1145]: Cf. Yt. XIV, 33.

[^1146]: Zarathuśtra's wife.

[^1147]: Bangha; the so-called Bang of Zoroaster (Vend. XV, 14 \[44\]; Phl. tr.). What must have been its virtue may be gathered from the legends of Gūśtāsp and Ardā Vīrāf, who are said to have been transported in soul to the heavens, and to have had the higher [pg 268] mysteries revealed to them, on drinking from a cup prepared by the prophet (Zarduśt Nāmah), or from a cup of Gūśtāsp-bang (Ardā Vīrāf, II, 29).

[^1148]: The itinerant priests, the ancestors of the modern dervishes.

[^1149]: Or better, do sacrifice; cf. Yt. XIV, 39.

* * *

[pg 270]

## XVII. ASHI YAŚT.


_May Ahura Mazda be rejoiced! . . . ._ {#XVIII:0}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_I confess myself a worshipper of Mazda, a follower of Zarathuśtra, one who hates the Daēvas and obeys the laws of Ahura;_

_For sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification unto \[Hāvani\], the holy and master of holiness . . . ._

Unto the Glory of the Aryans, made by Mazda, Be propitiation, with sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification.

_Yathā ahū vairyō; The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

Ahura Mazda spake unto Spitama Zarathuśtra, saying: 'I made the Aryan Glory, rich in food, rich in flocks, rich in wealth [^1190], rich in Glory; provided with full store of intelligence, with full store of money, to withstand Need, and to withstand enemies. {#XVIII:1}

[pg 284]

'It destroys Angra Mainyu, who is all death: it destroys Aēshma, the fiend of the wounding spear [^1191]; it destroys the yellow Būshyãsta [^1192]; it destroys the contagion [^1193] of Aēkha [^1194]; it destroys the fiend of death, Apaosha [^1195]; it destroys the non-Aryan nations. {#XVIII:2}

'And I made the great Ashi Vanguhi; she comes in, amid the family; she comes in, inside the fine royal palace [^1196]. {#XVIII:3}

'Let Ashi, with fulness of welfare, follow the man who gladdens the faithful with his gifts [^1197]! she comes in, inside his family; she comes in, inside his fine royal palace. {#XVIII:4}

'With all sorts of flocks, with all victory, with all intelligence, with all Glory, the great Ashi Vanguhi puts one foot [^1198] inside his family; she comes in, inside his fine royal palace.

'Horses multiply a thousandfold, flocks multiply a thousandfold; and so does his virtuous offspring, (as) the bright, glorious star Tiśtrya moves on equally [^1199], and so does the strong wind made by Mazda, and so does the Glory of the Aryas. {#XVIII:5}

'And they bring increase on the tops of all mountains, down the depths of all vales; they bring increase to all the growing plants [^1200], the fair, the golden-hued. And they bring (away) [^1201] the contagion [pg 285] of Aēkha, they bring (away) the fiend of death, Apaosha. {#XVIII:6}

'Hail to the bright and glorious star Tiśtrya! Hail to the strong wind, made by Mazda! Hail to the Glory of the Aryas! {#XVIII:7}

_'Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good. . . . ._

'We worship the Ahuna Vairya. {#XVIII:8}

'We worship Asha-Vahiśta, the fairest Amesha Speṇta.

'We worship the rightly-spoken Words [^1202], fiend-smiting and healing.

'We worship the healing, well-spoken Words, the fiend-smiting.

'We worship the Mãthra Speṇta and the Law of Mazda, and (piety) that delights in Haoma [^1203]. We worship the Glory of the Aryas.

_'Yēṇhē hātãm: All those beings of whom Ahura Mazda . . . ._

_'Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._ {#XVIII:9}

'I bless the sacrifice and prayer, and the strength and vigour of the Glory of the Aryas, made by Mazda.

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_'\[Give\] unto that man [^1204] brightness and glory, . . give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones.'_

[^1190]: As it gives food, flocks, and wealth to those who get possessed of it.

[^1191]: See Vendīdād, Introd. IV, 22.

[^1192]: Ibid. Introd. IV, 24.

[^1193]: Doubtful.

[^1194]: ? A daēva or a disease.

[^1195]: See Yt. VIII, 22.

[^1196]: See Yt. XVII.

[^1197]: Who gives alms to the poor Mazdayasnians.

[^1198]: Even one foot (?), when she stays not there 'for long friendship' (Yt. XVII, 6).

[^1199]: So that the rain falls in due time (Yt. VIII, 11).

[^1200]: Cf. Yt. VIII, 29.

[^1201]: Cf. § 2.

[^1202]: Arshukhdha vacō, the words conformable to the rites.

[^1203]: Haomacinem; see Études Iraniennes, II, 148.

[^1204]: Who shall have sacrificed to the Aryan Glory.

* * *

[pg 286]

## XIX. ZAMYĀD YAŚT.


_May Ahura Mazda be rejoiced! . . . ._ {#XIX:0}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . ._

_I confess myself a worshipper of Mazda, a follower of Zarathuśtra, one who hates the Daēvas and obeys the laws of Ahura;_

_For sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification unto \[Hāvani\], the holy and master of holiness . . . ._

Unto Mount Ushi-darena, made by Mazda, the seat of holy happiness; unto the kingly Glory, made by Mazda; unto that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, made by Mazda [^1205], [pg 287] Be propitiation, with sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification.

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

#### I.

The first mountain that rose up out of the earth, O Spitama Zarathuśtra! was the Haraiti Barez [^1206]. That mountain stretches all along the shores of the land washed by waters [^1207] towards the east. {#XIX:1}

The second mountain was Mount Zeredhō, outside [^1208] Mount Manusha [^1209]: this mountain too stretches all along the shores of the land washed by waters towards the east.

From there grew up Mount Ushi-dhāu Ushi-darena [^1210], Mount Erezifya [^1211], and Mount Fraorepa. {#XIX:2}

The sixth was Mount Erezura [^1212].

The seventh was Mount Bumya [^1213].

The eighth was Mount Raoidhita [^1214].

[pg 288]

The ninth was Mount Maziśiśvāu.

The tenth was Mount Aṇtare-danghu.

The eleventh was Mount Erezisha.

The twelfth was Mount Vāiti-gaēsa [^1215].

And Mount Ādarana, Mount Bayana, Mount Iśkata Upairi-saēna [^1216], with the . . . . [^1217] snows; the two Hamaṇkuna mountains, the eight Vasna mountains, the eight powerful Frāvaṇku, the four Vidhvana summits; {#XIX:3}

Mount Aēzakha, Mount Maēnakha, Mount Vākhedrakaē, Mount Asaya, Mount Tudhaskaē, Mount Iśavaē, Mount Draoshiśvāu, Mount Sāirivāu, Mount Nanghuśmāu, Mount Kakahyu, Mount Aṇtare-Kangha [^1218]; {#XIX:4}

Mount Sicidava [^1219], Mount Ahuna, Mount Raēmana, Mount Asha-stembana, Mount Urunyō-vāidhkaē, Mount Āsnavaṇṭ [^1220], Mount Ushaoma, Mount Uśta-hvarenah, Mount Syāmaka [^1221], Mount Vafrayāu, Mount Vourusha; [pg 289] 6\. Amongst which stand Mount Jatara, Mount Adhutavau, Mount Spitavarena, Mount Speṇtō-dāta [^1222], Mount Kadrva-aspa [^1223], Mount Kaoirisa [^1224], Mount Taēra [^1225], Mount Barō-srayana, Mount Barana, Mount Frāpayāu, Mount Udrya, and Mount Raēvaṇṭ [^1226], and all those heights to which men have given the name of mount, {#XIX:5}

To the number of two thousand mountains, and two hundred and forty and four [^1227], O Spitama Zarathuśtra! {#XIX:7}

For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice worth being heard, namely, unto the awful kingly Glory. Unto the awful kingly Glory we offer up the libations, the Haoma and meat, the baresma, the wisdom of the tongue, the holy spells, the speech, the deeds, the libations, and the rightly-spoken words [^1228]. {#XIX:8}

Yēṇhē hātãm: All those beings of whom Ahura Mazda [^1228] . . . .

#### II.

We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda; most conquering, highly working, that possesses health, wisdom, and happiness, and is more powerful to destroy than all other creatures; [pg 290] 10\. That belongs to Ahura Mazda, as (through it) Ahura Mazda made the creatures, many and good, many and fair, many and wonderful, many and prosperous, many and bright; {#XIX:9}

 [^1229]. So that they may restore the world, which will (thenceforth) never grow old and never die, never decaying and never rotting, ever living and ever increasing, and master of its wish, when the dead will rise, when life and immortality will come, and the world will be restored at its wish; {#XIX:11}

When the creation will grow deathless,—the prosperous creation of the Good Spirit,—and the Druj shall perish, though she may rush on every side to kill the holy beings; she and her hundredfold brood shall perish, as it is the will of the Lord [^1230]. {#XIX:12}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._ {#XIX:13}

#### III.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . . [^1231]_ {#XIX:14}

 [^1232]. That belongs to the Amesha-Speṇtas, the bright ones, whose looks perform their wish, tall, quickly coming to do, strong, lordly, who are undecaying and holy; {#XIX:15}

Who are all seven of one thought, who are all seven of one speech, who are all seven of one deed; whose thought is the same, whose speech is the same, whose deed is the same, whose father and commander is the same, namely, the Maker, Ahura Mazda. {#XIX:16}

[pg 291]

Who see one another's soul thinking of good thoughts, thinking of good words, thinking of good deeds, thinking of Garō-nmāna, and whose ways are shining as they go down to the libations; {#XIX:17}

Who are the makers and governors, the shapers and overseers, the keepers and preservers of these creations of Ahura Mazda. {#XIX:18}

 [^1233]. It is they who shall restore the world, which will (thenceforth) never grow old and never die, never decaying and never rotting, ever living and ever increasing, and master of its wish, when the dead will rise, when life and immortality will come, and the world will be restored at its wish; {#XIX:19}

When the creation will grow deathless,—the prosperous creation of the Good Spirit,—and the Druj shall perish, though she may rush on every side to kill the holy beings; she and her hundredfold brood shall perish, as it is the will of the Lord. {#XIX:20}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### IV.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:21}

That belongs to the gods in the heavens and to those in the material world, and to the blessed ones, born or not yet born, who are to perform the restoration of the world [^1234]. {#XIX:22}

 [^1235]. It is they who shall restore the world, which will (thenceforth) never grow old and never die, never decaying and never rotting, ever living and [pg 292] ever increasing, and master of its wish, when the dead will rise, when life and immortality will come, and the world will be restored at its wish; {#XIX:23}

When the creation will grow deathless,—the prosperous creation of the Good Spirit,—and the Druj shall perish, though she may rush on every side to kill the holy beings; she and her hundredfold brood shall perish, as it is the will of the Lord. {#XIX:24}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### V.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:25}

That clave unto Haoshyangha, the Paradhāta, for a long time [^1236], when he ruled over the seven Karshvares of the earth, over the Daēvas and men, over the Yātus and the Pairikas, over the oppressors, the blind, and the deaf, he who smote two-thirds of the Daēvas of Māzana and of the Varenya fiends [^1237]. {#XIX:26}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### VI.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:27}

That clave unto Takhma Urupa, the well-armed, while he ruled over the seven Karshvares of the earth, over the Daēvas and men, the Yātus and Pairikas, the oppressors, the blind, and the deaf; {#XIX:28}

When he conquered all Daēvas and men, all the Yātus and Pairikas, and rode Angra Mainyu, [pg 293] turned into the shape of a horse, all around the earth from one end to the other, for thirty years [^1238]. {#XIX:29}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### VII.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:30}

That clave unto the bright Yima, the good shepherd, for a long time [^1239], while he ruled over the seven Karshvares of the earth, over the Daēvas and men, the Yātus and Pairikas, the oppressors, the blind, and the deaf; {#XIX:31}

He who took from the Daēvas both riches and welfare, both fatness and flocks, both weal and Glory [^1240]; {#XIX:32}

In whose reign both aliments [^1241] were never failing for feeding creatures, flocks and men were undying, waters and plants were undrying;

In whose reign there was neither cold wind nor hot wind, neither old age nor death, nor envy made by the Daēvas [^1242], in the times before his lie, before he began to have delight in words of falsehood and untruth. {#XIX:33}

But when he began to find delight in words of falsehood and untruth [^1243], the Glory was seen to flee away from him in the shape of a bird. When his Glory had disappeared, then the great [^1244] Yima [pg 294] Khshaēta the good shepherd, trembled and was in sorrow before his foes [^1245]; he was confounded, and laid him down on the ground. {#XIX:34}

The first time [^1246] when the Glory departed from the bright Yima, the Glory went from Yima, the son of Vīvanghaṇṭ, in the shape of a Vāraghna bird [^1247]. {#XIX:35}

Then Mithra seized that Glory, Mithra, the lord of wide pastures, whose ear is quick to hear, who has a thousand senses. We sacrifice unto Mithra, the lord of all countries, whom Ahura Mazda has created the most glorious of all the gods in the heavens.

The second time when the Glory departed from the bright Yima, the Glory went from Yima, the son of Vīvanghaṇṭ, in the shape of a Vāraghna bird. {#XIX:36}

Then Thraētaona seized that Glory, he, the heir of the valiant Āthwya clan, who was the most victorious of all victorious men next to Zarathuśtra;

Who smote Aži Dahāka, the three-mouthed, the three-headed, the six-eyed, who had a thousand senses, that most powerful, fiendish Druj; that demon baleful to the world, the strongest Druj that Angra Mainyu created against the material world, to destroy the world of the good principle [^1248]. {#XIX:37}

[pg 295]

The third time when the Glory departed from the bright Yima, that Glory went from Yima, the son of Vīvanghaṇṭ, in the shape of a Vāraghna bird. Then the manly-hearted Keresāspa [^1249] seized that Glory; he who was the sturdiest of the men of strength, next to Zarathuśtra, for his manly courage. {#XIX:38}

For Manly Courage clave unto him. We worship Manly Courage, firm or foot, unsleeping, quick to rise, and fully awake, that clave unto Keresāspa; {#XIX:39}

Who killed the snake Srvara, the horse-devouring, men-devouring, yellow, poisonous snake, over which yellow poison flowed a thumb's breadth thick. Upon him Keresāspa was cooking his food in a brass vessel: at the time of noon, the fiend felt the heat, and stood upon his feet: he rushed from under the brass vessel and upset the boiling water: the manly-hearted Keresāspa fell back affrighted [^1250]; {#XIX:40}

Who killed the golden-heeled Gaṇdarewa, that was rushing with open jaws, eager to destroy the living world of the good principle [^1251]; {#XIX:41}

Who killed the brood of Pathana, all the nine [^1252]; [pg 296] and the brood of Nivika, and the brood of Dāśtayana;

Who killed the golden-crowned Hitāspa [^1253], and Vareshava, the son of Dāna [^1254], and Pitaona, attended by many Pairikas [^1255];

Who killed Arezō-shamana, him of the manly courage, who was strong, well-beloved [^1256], hail, energetically rushing, fully awake, never falling back. . . . [^1257]; {#XIX:42}

Who killed Snāvidhaka, him who killed with his nails, the stone-handed: thus did he exclaim to all around: 'I am an infant still, I am not yet of age: if I ever grow of age, I shall make the earth a wheel, I shall make the heavens a chariot; {#XIX:43}

'I shall bring down the Good Spirit from the shining Garō-nmāna; I shall make the Evil Spirit rush up from the dreary Hell. They will carry my [pg 297] chariot, both the Good Spirit and the Evil One, unless the manly-hearted Keresāspa kill me.' {#XIX:44}

The manly-hearted Keresāspa killed him, his life went away, his spirit vanished [^1258].

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### VIII.

_We sacrifice unto the awful Glory, that cannot be forcibly seized [^1259], made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:45}

For which the Good Spirit and the Evil One did struggle with one another [^1260]: for that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized [^1259] they flung each of them. their darts most swift. {#XIX:46}

The Good Spirit flung a dart, and so did Vohu-Manō, and Asha-Vahiśta and Ātar, the son of Ahura Mazda.

The Evil Spirit flung a dart, and so did Akem-Manō [^1261], and Aēshma of the wounding spear, and Aži Dahāka and Spityura, he who sawed Yima in twain [^1262].

[pg 298]

Then forward came Ātar [^1263], the son of Ahura Mazda, thinking thus in his heart: 'I want to seize that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized.' {#XIX:47}

But Aži Dahāka, the three-mouthed, he of the evil law, rushed on his back, thinking of extinguishing it:

'Here give it up to me [^1264], O Ātar, son of Ahura Mazda: if thou seizest that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, I shall rush upon thee, so that thou mayest never more blaze on the earth made by Ahura and protect the world of the good principle.' {#XIX:48}

And Ātar took back his hands, as the instinct of life prevailed, so much had Aži affrighted him.

Then Aži, the three-mouthed, he of the evil law, rushed forward, thinking thus in his heart: 'I want to seize that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized.' {#XIX:49}

But Ātar, the son of Ahura Mazda, advanced behind him, speaking in these words:

'There give it up to me [^1264], thou three-mouthed Aži Dahāka. If thou seizest that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, then I will enter thy hinder part, I will blaze up in thy jaws, so that thou mayest never more rush upon the earth made by Mazda and destroy the world of the good principle.' {#XIX:50}

Then Aži took back his hands, as the instinct of life prevailed, so much had Ātar affrighted him.

That Glory swells up and goes to the sea [pg 299] Vouru-Kasha. The swift-horsed Son of the Waters [^1265] seizes it at once: this is the wish of the Son of the Waters, the swift-horsed: 'I want to seize that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, down to the bottom of the sea Vouru-Kasha, in the bottom of the deep rivers.' {#XIX:51}

We sacrifice unto the Son of the Waters, the swift-horsed, the tall and shining lord, the lord of females; the male god, who helps one at his appeal; who made man, who shaped man [^1266], a god who lives beneath waters, and whose ear is the quickest to hear when he is worshipped. {#XIX:52}

'And whosoever of you, O men,'—thus said Ahura Mazda,—'O holy Zarathuśtra! shall seize that Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, he has the gifts [^1267] of an Āthravan [^1268]; whosoever shall long for the illumination of knowledge, he has the gifts of an Āthravan; whosoever shall long for fulness of knowledge, he has the gifts of an Āthravan; {#XIX:53}

'And Riches will cleave unto him, giving him full welfare, holding a shield before him, powerful, rich of cattle and garments; and Victory will cleave unto him, day after day; and likewise Strength, that smites more than a year. Attended by that Victory, he will conquer the havocking hordes; attended by that Victory, he will conquer all those who hate him.' {#XIX:54}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

[pg 300]

#### IX.

_We sacrifice unto the awful Glory, that cannot be forcibly seized, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:55}

Which the Turanian ruffian Frangrasyan tried to seize in the sea Vouru-Kasha. He stripped himself naked, wishing to seize that Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra [^1269]. But the Glory escaped, the Glory fled away, the Glory changed its seat, and an arm of the sea Vouru-Kasha was produced, namely, that lake that is called Lake Husravah [^1270]. {#XIX:56}

 [^1271]. Then the most crafty Turanian Frangrasyan rushed out of the sea Vouru-Kasha, O Spitama Zarathuśtra! thinking evil thoughts: '. . . . [^1272] I have not been able to conquer the Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra. {#XIX:57}

'Then I will defile all corn and liquors [^1273], as to greatness, goodness, and fairness.' {#XIX:58}

—'Ahura Mazda will come against thee, ever eager to create new creatures [^1274].'

Then the most crafty Turanian Frangrasyan rushed down into the sea Vouru-Kasha, O Spitama Zarathuśtra!

[pg 301]

A second time he stripped himself naked, wishing to seize that Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra. But the Glory escaped, the Glory fled away, the Glory changed its seat, and an arm of the sea Vouru-Kasha was produced, namely, that lake that is called Lake Vanghazdāu [^1275]. {#XIX:59}

 [^1276]. Then the most crafty Turanian Frangrasyan rushed out of the sea Vouru-Kasha, O Spitama Zarathuśtra! thinking evil thoughts: '. . . . [^1277] I have not been able to conquer the Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra. {#XIX:60}

'Then I will defile all corn and liquors, as to greatness, goodness, and fairness.' {#XIX:61}

—'Ahura Mazda will come against thee, ever eager to create new creatures.'

Then the most crafty Turanian Frangrasyan rushed down into the sea Vouru-Kasha.

A third time he stripped himself naked, wishing to seize the Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra. But the Glory escaped, the Glory fled away, the Glory changed its seat, and an arm was produced in the sea Vouru-Kasha, namely, the water that is called Awž-dānva. {#XIX:62}

 [^1278]. Then the most crafty Turanian Frangrasyan rushed out of the sea Vouru-Kasha, O Spitama Zarathuśtra! thinking evil thoughts: '. . . . [^1279] I have [pg 302] not been able to conquer the Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra!' {#XIX:63}

He was not able to seize the Glory that belongs to the Aryan nations, born and unborn, and to the holy Zarathuśtra. {#XIX:64}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### X.

_We sacrifice unto the awful Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:65}

That cleaves unto him [^1280] who grows up there, where lies Lake Kãsava [^1281], along with the Haētumaṇṭ [^1282] river; there where stands Mount Ushidhāu [^1283], surrounded by waters, that run from the mountain. {#XIX:66}

It [^1284] runs unto him, it flows and swells unto him, bringing good pastures and fine horses, bringing plenty, full of glory; with beauty and weal; powerful and friendly, rich of pastures, prolific and golden. It runs unto him, it flows and swells unto him, bright and glorious, making the white . . . . [^1285] grow, smiting away all plagues. {#XIX:67}

And there comes with him a horse's strength, there comes with him a camel's strength, there [pg 303] comes with him a man's strength, there comes with him the kingly Glory: and there is in him, O holy Zarathuśtra! so much of kingly Glory as might extinguish at once all the non-Aryan nations. {#XIX:68}

And then (through it) living creatures may keep away [^1286] hunger and death, living creatures (may keep away) cold and heat [^1286]. Such is the kingly Glory, the keeper of the Aryan nations and of the five kinds of animals [^1287], made to help the faithful and the Law of the worshippers of Mazda. {#XIX:69}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### XI.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:70}

That clave unto Kavi Kavāta, and unto Kavi Aipivōhu, and unto Kavi Usadha, and unto Kavi Arshan, and unto Kavi Pisina, and unto Kavi Byārshan, and unto Kavi Syāvarshan [^1288]; {#XIX:71}

So that they were all of them brave, all of them strong, all of them healthful, all of them wise, all of them happy in their wishes, all of them powerful kings. {#XIX:72}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### XII.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:73}

 [^1289]. That clave unto Kavi Husravah for the well-shapen Strength, for the Victory made by Ahura, for the crushing Ascendant; for the righteousness of the law, for the innocence of the law, for the [pg 304] unconquerable power of the law; for the extermination of the enemies at one stroke; {#XIX:74}

And for the vigour of health, for the Glory made by Mazda, for the health of the body, and for a good, virtuous offspring, wise, chief in assemblies, bright, and clear-eyed, that frees \[their father\] from the pangs \[of hell\], of good intellect; and for that part in the blessed world that falls to wisdom and to those who do not follow impiety; {#XIX:75}

And for a dominion full of splendour, for a long, long life, and for all boons and remedies; {#XIX:76}

So that king Husravah \[had the lead\] all along the long race, and he could not pass through the forest, he [^1290], the murderer, who was fiercely striving against him on horseback; the lord Kavi Husravah prevailed over all; he put in bonds Frangrasyan and Keresavazda [^1291], to avenge the murder of his father Syāvarshāna, a man, and of Aghraēratha, a semi-man [^1292]. {#XIX:77}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### XIII.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:78}

That clave unto the holy Zarathuśtra, so that he thought according to the Law, spake according [pg 305] to the Law, and did according to the Law; so that he was the holiest in holiness in all the living world, the best-ruling in exercising rule, the brightest in brightness, the most glorious in glory, the most victorious in victory. {#XIX:79}

At his sight the Daēvas rushed away; at his sight the (demoniac) malices were extinguished; at his sight the Jainis [^1293] drew back their ways from the mortals and, lamenting [^1294] and wailing, laid violent hands on the Daēvas. {#XIX:80}

And that one prayer, the Ahuna Vairya, which the holy Zarathuśtra sang and repeated four times, with a song that waxed louder and louder, drove back all the Daēvas beneath the earth, and took off from them sacrifice and prayer [^1295]. {#XIX:81}

It was it, the Glory of Zarathuśtra, that the Turanian ruffian Frangrasyan tried to seize to rule over all the Karshvares; round about the seven Karshvares did that ruffian Frangrasyan rush, trying to seize the Glory of Zarathuśtra [^1296]. But that Glory escaped to hidden inlets of the sea [^1297]; and there those two [^1298] made my will [^1299] roll on [^1300]; they entered my will, as it was my wish, Ahura Mazda's, and as it was the wish of the Law of Mazda. {#XIX:82}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

[pg 306]

#### XIV.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:83}

That clave unto king Vīśtāspa, so that he thought according to the Law, spake according to the Law, and did according to the Law; so that he professed that Law, destroying his foes and causing the Daēvas to retire. {#XIX:84}

 [^1301]. Who, driving the Druj before him [^1302], sought wide room for the holy religion; who, driving the Druj before him, made wide room for the holy religion; who made himself the arm and support of this law of Ahura, of this law of Zarathuśtra; {#XIX:85}

Who took her, standing bound, from the hands of the Hunus, and established her to sit in the middle \[of the world\], high ruling, never falling back, holy, nourished with plenty of cattle and pastures, blessed with plenty of cattle and pastures. {#XIX:86}

The valiant king Vīśtāspa conquered all enemies, Tãthravaṇṭ of the evil law, Peshana, the worshipper of the Daēvas, and the fiendish wicked Arejaṭ-aspa and the other wicked Hvyaonas [^1303]. {#XIX:87}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### XV.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:88}

 [^1304]. That will cleave unto the victorious Saoshyaṇṭ and his helpers [^1305], when he shall restore the [pg 307] world, which will (thenceforth) never grow old and never die, never decaying and never rotting, ever living and ever increasing, and master of its wish, when the dead will rise, when life and immortality will come, and the world will be restored at its wish; {#XIX:89}

When the creation will grow deathless,—the prosperous creation of the Good Spirit,—and the Druj shall perish, though she may rush on every side to kill the holy beings; she and her hundredfold brood shall perish, as it is the will of the Lord. {#XIX:90}

_For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . ._

#### XVI.

_We sacrifice unto the awful kingly Glory, made by Mazda . . . ._ {#XIX:91}

When Astvaṭ-ereta [^1306] shall rise up from Lake Kãsava [^1307], a friend of Ahura Mazda, a son of Vīspa-taurvairi [^1308], knowing the victorious knowledge. {#XIX:92}

It was that Glory that Thraētaona bore with him when Aži Dahāka was killed [^1309];

That Frangrasyan, the Turanian, bore when Drvāu [^1310] was killed, when the Bull was killed [^1311]; {#XIX:93}

That king Husravah bore when Frangrasyan, the Turanian, was killed [^1312]; [pg 308] That king Vīśtāspa bore, when he victoriously maintained Holiness against the host of the fiends and took off the Drub from the world of the good principle [^1313].

He [^1314], with the eye of intelligence [^1315], shall look down upon all the creatures of the Paēśiś [^1316], her of the evil seed: he shall look upon the whole living world with the eye of plenty, and his look shall deliver to immortality the whole of the living creatures. {#XIX:94}

And there shall his friends [^1317] come forward, the friends of Astvaṭ-ereta, who are fiend-smiting, well-thinking, well-speaking, well-doing, following the good law, and whose tongues have never uttered a word of falsehood. {#XIX:95}

Before them shall Aēshma of the wounding spear, who has no Glory, bow and flee; he shall smite the most wicked Druj, her of the evil seed, born of darkness.

Akem-Manō [^1318] smites, but Vohu-Manō shall smite him; the Word of falsehood smites, but the Word of truth shall smite it. Haurvatāṭ and Ameretāṭ [^1319] shall smite both hunger and thirst: Haurvatāṭ and Ameretāṭ shall smite the evil hunger and the evil thirst. The evil-doing Angra Mainyu bows and flees, becoming powerless. {#XIX:96}

For its brightness and glory, I will offer it a sacrifice . . . .

Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . . {#XIX:97}

[pg 309]

I bless the sacrifice and prayer, and the strength and vigour of Mount Ushi-darena, made by Mazda, the seat of holy happiness; of the kingly Glory, made by Mazda; of the Glory that cannot be forcibly seized, made by Mazda [^1320].

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_\[Give\] unto that man [^1321] brightness and glory, . . . . give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones._

[^1246]: The Glory is described as departing three times, because it is threefold, according as it belongs to the king considered as a priest, a warrior, or a husbandman. In that threefold character it is identical with Ādar Frobā, Ādar Gushasp, and Ādar Būrzīn Mihr ([p. 7](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#page_7), notes).

[^1250]: Cf. Yasna IX, II (34-39). This tale belongs to the widespread cyclus of the island-whale (a whale whose back is mistaken by sailors for an island; they land upon it, cook their food there, and the monster. awaked by the heat, flies off and carries them away: see Arabian Nights, Seventy-first Night; Babā Bathrā, 5).

[^1251]: See Yt. V, 38.

[^1252]: Known in the Minokhired (XXVII, 50) as 'the wolf Kapōḍ' (perhaps 'the blue wolf,' as Mr. West suggests), 'which they also call Pehan.' Those nine sons of Pathana were nine highwaymen (the very word Pathana seems to have that meaning): their defeat is told by Keresāspa in a Pahlavi Rivāyat as follows: 'I have slain the highwaymen who were so big in body that, when they were [pg 296] walking, people considered in this way, that "below them are the stars and moon, and below them moves the sun at dawn, and the water of the sea reaches up to their knees." And I reached up to their legs, and they were smitten on the legs by me; they fell, and the hills on the earth were shattered by them' (West, Pahlavi Texts, II, 376). Keresāspa's Fravashi, accordingly, is invoked against thieves (Yt. XIII, 136). Perhaps the assimilation of the wolf Kapōḍ with Pehan is merely a guess of the author of the Minokhired.

XIV, 30), which might induce us to identify Vareshava with the gigantic bird Kamak, 'which overshadowed the earth and kept off the rain till the rivers dried up' (West, l.l. 378), and whose destruction was one of the feats of Keresāspa.

    'Such were they youths! Had they to manhood grown,
     Almighty Jove had trembled on his throne:
     But ere the harvest of the beard began
     To bristle on the chin, and promise man,
     His shafts Apollo aim’d.' (Pope.)

[^1259]: The sacerdotal Glory; see [p. 11](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#page_11), note [6](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#fn_78), cf. § 53.

Nothing more is known of him, though he appears to have played a great part in the original Yima legend, and to have stood to his brother in the same relation as Barmāyūn and Katāyūn to Ferīdūn, or [pg 298] Shagād to Rustam. Firdausi does not mention him, and makes Dahāk himself saw Jemshīd.

[^1280]: That is to say, to any one who . . . . The Kavis or Kings of Iran are meant: Lake Kãsava was supposed to be 'the home of the Kayān race' (Bund. XXI, 7). The Kavis are enumerated in the following clauses (§§ 71 seq.).

[^1287]: See [p. 182](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2318.htm#page_182), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2318.htm#fn_817).
