[pg 310]

## XX. VANAṆṬ YAŚT.


_May Ahura Mazda be rejoiced! . . . ._ {#XX:0}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . ._

_I confess myself a worshipper of Mazda, a follower of Zarathuśtra, one who hates the Daēvas and obeys the laws of Ahura;_

_For sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification unto \[Hāvani\], the holy and master of holiness . . . ._

Unto the star Vanaṇṭ, made by Mazda,

Be propitiation, with sacrifice, prayer, propitiation, and glorification.

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

We sacrifice unto the star Vanaṇṭ, made by Mazda, the holy and master of holiness. {#XX:1}

I will sacrifice unto Vanaṇṭ, strong, invoked by his own name [^1322], healing, in order to withstand the accursed and most foul Khrafstras [^1323] of the most abominable Angra Mainyu.

_Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._ {#XX:2}

I bless the sacrifice and prayer, and the strength and vigour of the star Vanaṇṭ, made by Mazda.

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_\[Give\] unto that man [^1324] brightness and glory, . . . . give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones._

[^1322]: See [p. 13](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#page_13), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2304.htm#fn_96).

[^1323]: The reptiles and other Ahrimanian creatures (Vendīdād, Introd. V, 11) which are destroyed by the rain (Bund. VII, 7).

[^1324]: Who sacrifices to Vanaṇṭ.

* * *

[pg 311]

### XXI AND XXII. YAŚT FRAGMENTS.

_These two Yaśts or Yaśt fragments are known among the Parsis as the Hādhōkht Nask, though their context does not correspond to any part of the description of that Nask as given in the Dīn-kart (West, Pahlavi Texts, I, 224, note 8). A Pahlavi translation of these Yaśts has been edited by Haug and West (The Book of Ardā Vīrāf, p. 269 seq.)._

## XXI. YAŚT FRAGMENT.


Zarathuśtra asked Ahura Mazda: 'O Ahura Mazda, most beneficent Spirit, Maker of the material world, thou Holy One! {#XXI:1}

What is the only word in which is contained the glorification of all good things, of all the things that are the offspring of the good principle?'

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is the praise of Holiness [^1325], O Spitama Zarathuśtra! {#XXI:2}

'He who recites the praise of Holiness [^1325], in the fulness of faith and with a devoted heart, praises me, Ahura Mazda; he praises the waters, he praises the earth, he praises the cattle, he praises the plants, he praises all good things made by Mazda, all the things that are the offspring of the good principle. {#XXI:3}

'For the reciting of that word of truth, O Zarathuśtra! the pronouncing of that formula, the Ahuna Vairya, increases strength and victory in one's soul and piety. {#XXI:4}

[pg 312]

'For that only recital of the praise of Holiness is worth a hundred khshnaothras of the beings of Holiness [^1326], when delivered while going to sleep, a thousand when delivered after eating, ten thousand when delivered during cohabitation, or any number when delivered in departing this life.' {#XXI:5}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth ten others in greatness, goodness, and fairness? {#XXI:6}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers when eating the gifts of Haurvatāṭ and Ameretāṭ [^1327], at the same time professing good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, and rejecting evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds.' {#XXI:7}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth a hundred others in greatness, goodness, and fairness?' {#XXI:8}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers while drinking of the Haoma strained for the sacrifice, at the same time professing good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, and rejecting evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds.' {#XXI:9}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth a thousand others in greatness, goodness, and fairness?' {#XXI:10}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers when starting [pg 313] up from his bed or going to sleep again, at the same time professing good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, and rejecting evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds.' {#XXI:11}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth ten thousand others in greatness, goodness, and fairness?' {#XXI:12}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers when waking up and rising from sleep, at the same time professing good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, and rejecting evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds.' {#XXI:13}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth this Karshvare of ours, Hvaniratha [^1328], with its cattle and its chariots, without its men, in greatness, goodness, and fairness?' {#XXI:14}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers in the last moments of his life, at the same time professing good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, and rejecting evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds.' {#XXI:15}

'What is the one recital of the praise of Holiness that is worth all that is between the earth and the heavens, and this earth, and that luminous space, and all the good things made by Mazda, that are the offspring of the good principle in greatness, goodness, and fairness?' {#XXI:16}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It is that one, O holy Zarathuśtra! that a man delivers to renounce evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds [^1329].' {#XXI:17}

[^1325]: Asha: the Ashem Vohū.

[^1326]: A hundred times the formula: 'Be propitiation (khshnaothra) unto N. . . ., the holy and master of holiness' (cf. [p. 1](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2303.htm#page_1), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2303.htm#fn_3)).

[^1327]: Eating or drinking (see Vendīdād, Introd. IV, 33).

[^1328]: See [p. 123](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2315.htm#page_123), note [5](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2315.htm#fn_575).

[^1329]: In a conversion, or in the recital of the penitential prayers.

* * *

[pg 314]

## XXII. YAŚT XXII.


#### I.

Zarathuśtra asked Ahura Mazda: 'O Ahura Mazda, most beneficent Spirit, Maker of the material world, thou Holy One! {#XXII:1}

'When one of the faithful departs this life, where does his soul abide on that night?'

Ahura Mazda answered:

'It takes its seat near the head, singing the Uśtavaiti Gātha [^1331] and proclaiming happiness: "Happy is he, happy the man, whoever he be, to whom Ahura Mazda gives the full accomplishment of his wishes!" On that night his soul tastes [^1332] as much of pleasure as the whole of the living world can taste.' [pg 315] 3\. —'On the second night where does his soul abide? {#XXII:2}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It takes its seat near the head, singing the Uśtavaiti Gātha and proclaiming happiness: "Happy is he, happy the man, whoever he be, to whom Ahura Mazda gives the full accomplishment of his wishes!" On that night his soul tastes as much of pleasure as the whole of the living world can taste.' {#XXII:4}

—'On the third night where does his soul abide? {#XXII:5}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It takes its seat near the head, singing the Uśtavaiti Gātha and proclaiming happiness: "Happy is he, happy the man, whoever he be, to whom Ahura Mazda gives the full accomplishment of his wishes!" On that night his soul tastes as much of pleasure as the whole of the living world can taste.' {#XXII:6}

At the end [^1333] of the third night, when the dawn appears, it seems to the soul of the faithful one as if it were brought amidst plants and scents: it seems as if a wind were blowing from the region of the south, from the regions of the south, a sweet-scented wind, sweeter-scented than any other wind in the world. {#XXII:7}

And it seems to the soul of the faithful one as if he were inhaling that wind with the nostrils, and he thinks: 'Whence does that wind blow, the sweetest-scented wind I ever inhaled with my nostrils? {#XXII:8}

And it seems to him as if his own conscience were advancing to him in that wind, in the shape of a maiden fair, bright, white-armed, strong, tall-formed, [pg 316] high-standing, thick-breasted, beautiful of body, noble, of a glorious seed [^1334], of the size of a maid in her fifteenth year, as fair as the fairest things in the world. {#XXII:9}

And the soul of the faithful one addressed her, asking: 'What maid art thou, who art the fairest maid I have ever seen?' {#XXII:10}

And she, being his own conscience, answers him: 'O thou youth of good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, of good religion, I am thy own conscience! {#XXII:11}

'Everybody did love thee for that greatness, goodness, fairness, sweet-scentedness, victorious strength and freedom from sorrow, in which thou dost appear to me;

'And so thou, O youth of good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, of good religion! didst love me for that greatness, goodness, fairness, sweet-scentedness, victorious strength, and freedom from sorrow, in which I appear to thee. {#XXII:12}

'When thou wouldst see a man making derision [^1335] and deeds of idolatry, or rejecting [^1336] (the poor) and shutting his door [^1337], then thou wouldst sit singing the Gāthas and worshipping the good waters and Ātar, the son of Ahura Mazda, and rejoicing [^1338] the faithful that would come from near or from afar. {#XXII:13}

[pg 317]

'I was lovely and thou madest me still lovelier; I was fair and thou madest me still fairer; I was desirable and thou madest me still more desirable; I was sitting in a forward place and thou madest me sit in the foremost place, through this good thought, through this good speech, through this good deed of thine; and so henceforth men worship me for my having long sacrificed unto and conversed with Ahura Mazda. {#XXII:14}

'The first step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Thought [^1339] Paradise; {#XXII:15}

'The second step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Word [^1340] Paradise;

'The third step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Deed [^1341] Paradise;

'The fourth step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Endless Lights [^1342].'

Then one of the faithful, who had departed before him, asked him, saying: 'How didst thou depart this life, thou holy man? How didst thou come, thou holy man! from the abodes full of cattle and full of the wishes and enjoyments of love? From the material world into the world of the spirit? From the decaying world into the undecaying one? How long did thy felicity last?' {#XXII:16}

And Ahura Mazda answered: 'Ask him not what thou askest him, who has just gone the dreary [pg 318] way, full of fear and distress, where the body and the soul part from one another. {#XXII:17}

'\[Let him eat\] of the food brought to him, of the oil of Zaremaya [^1343]: this is the food for the youth of good thoughts, of good words, of good deeds, of good religion, after he has departed this life; this is the food for the holy woman, rich in good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, well-principled and obedient to her husband, after she has departed this life.' {#XXII:18}

#### II.

Zarathuśtra asked Ahura Mazda: 'O Ahura Mazda, most beneficent Spirit, Maker of the material world, thou Holy One! {#XXII:19}

'When one of the wicked perishes, where does his soul abide on that night?'

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It rushes and sits near the skull, singing the Kima [^1344] Gātha, O holy Zarathuśtra! {#XXII:20}

' "To what land shall I turn, O Ahura Mazda? To whom shall I go with praying?"

'On that night his soul tastes as much of suffering as the whole of the living world can taste.'

—'On the second night, where does his soul abide?' {#XXII:21}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It rushes and sits near the skull, singing the Kima Gātha, O holy [pg 319] Zarathuśtra! "To what land shall I turn, O Ahura Mazda? To whom shall I go with praying?" {#XXII:22}

'On that night his soul tastes as much of suffering as the whole of the living world can taste.'

—'On the third night, where does his soul abide?' {#XXII:23}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'It rushes and sits near the skull, singing the Kima Gātha, O holy Zarathuśtra! "To what land shall I turn, O Ahura Mazda? To whom shall I go with praying?" {#XXII:24}

'On that night his soul tastes as much of suffering as the whole of the living world can taste.'

At the end of the third night, O holy Zarathuśtra! when the dawn appears, it seems to the soul of the faithless one as if it were brought amidst snow and stench, and as if a wind were blowing from the region of the north, from the regions of the north, a foul-scented wind, the foulest-scented of all the winds in the world. {#XXII:25}

-32. And it seems to the soul of the wicked man as if he were inhaling that wind with the nostrils, and he thinks: 'Whence does that wind blow, the foulest-scented wind that I ever inhaled with my nostrils [^1345]?' [pg 320] 33\. The first step that the soul of the wicked man made laid him in the Evil-Thought Hell; {#XXII:26}

The second step that the soul of the wicked man made laid him in the Evil-Word Hell;

The third step that the soul of the wicked man made laid him in the Evil-Deed Hell;

The fourth step that the soul of the wicked man made laid him in the Endless Darkness.

Then one of the wicked who departed before him addressed him, saying: 'How didst thou perish, O wicked man? How didst thou come, O fiend! from the abodes full of cattle and full of the wishes and enjoyments of love? From the material world into the world of the Spirit? From the decaying [pg 321] world into the undecaying one? How long did thy suffering last?' {#XXII:34}

Angra Mainyu, the lying one, said: 'Ask him not what thou askest him, who has just gone the dreary way, full of fear and distress, where the body and the soul part from one another. {#XXII:35}

'Let him eat of the food brought unto him, of poison and poisonous stench [^1346]: this is the food, after he has perished, for the youth of evil thoughts, evil words, evil deeds, evil religion after he has perished; this is the food for the fiendish woman, rich in evil thoughts, evil words, and evil deeds, evil religion, ill-principled, and disobedient to her husband. {#XXII:36}

 [^1347]. 'We worship the Fravashi of the holy man, whose name is Asmō-hvanvaṇṭ [^1348]; then I will worship the Fravashis of the other holy Ones who were strong of faith [^1349]. {#XXII:37}

 [^1347]. 'We worship the memory of Ahura Mazda, to keep the Holy Word. {#XXII:38}

'We worship the understanding of Ahura Mazda, to study the Holy Word.

'We worship the tongue of Ahura Mazda, to speak forth the Holy Word.

'We worship the mountain that gives understanding, that preserves understanding; \[we worship [pg 322] it\] by day and by night, with offerings of libations well-accepted [^1350].

 [^1351]. 'O Maker! how do the souls of the dead, the Fravashis of the holy Ones, manifest [^1352] themselves [^1353]?' {#XXII:39}

Ahura Mazda answered: 'They manifest themselves from goodness of spirit and excellence of mind [^1354].' {#XXII:40}

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

 [^1355]. Then towards the dawning of the dawn [^1356], that bird Parōdarś [^1357], that bird Karetō-dãsu [^1358] hears the voice of the Fire. {#XXII:41}

[pg 323]

Here the fiendish Būshyãsta, the long-handed, rushes from the region of the north, from the regions of the north, speaking thus, lying thus: 'Sleep on, O men! Sleep on, O sinners! Sleep on and live in sin.' {#XXII:42}

[^1330]: See , note [^1345].

[^1331]: The name of the second Gātha, which begins with the word uśta: the words in the text, 'Happy the man . . . .,' are its opening line (Yaśna XLII, 1).

[^1332]: Literally, sees, perceives.

[^1333]: Thraośta: in Pahlavi rōiśman.

[^1334]: 'That is to say, from the gods' (Pahl. Comm.).

[^1335]: Of holy things.

[^1336]: Doubtful. The Pahlavi commentary has the following gloss: 'He would not give his friends what they begged for.'

[^1337]: To the poor:—Urvarō-straya: urvar babāic kart (Pahl. Comm.): āighshān babā barā asrūnast (star, to tie, as in frastaretem baresma). Cf. Yt. XXIV, 37, 59.

[^1338]: With alms to the poor Mazdayasnians (ashō-dād).

[^1339]: The so-called Hūmat Paradise (cf. Yt. III, 3).

[^1340]: The so-called Hūkht Paradise.

[^1341]: The so-called Hvarsht Paradise.

[^1342]: The seat of the Garōthmān.

[^1343]: Zaremaya is the spring: the word translated oil (raoghna, Persian ![](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/img/31800.jpg)) might perhaps be better translated 'butter;' the milk made in the middle of spring was said to be the best (Vispērad I, 2; Pahl. Comm.; cf. Dādistān XXXI, 14).

[^1344]: The Gātha of lamenting, beginning with the word Kãm (Kãm nemē zãm: 'To what land shall I turn?'); Yasna XLVI (XLV).

[^1345]: A development similar to that in §§ 9-14 is to be supplied here: in the Ardā Vīrāf and the Minokhired the soul of the wicked is met by a horrid old woman, who is his own conscience: 'And in that wind he saw his own religion and deeds, as a profligate woman, naked, decayed, gaping, bandy-legged, lean-hipped, and unlimitedly spotted, so that spot was joined to spot, like the most hideous noxious creatures (khrafstar), most filthy and most stinking' (cf. § 9).

    Then that wicked soul spoke thus: 'Who art thou? than whom I never saw any one of the creatures of Aūharmazd and Akharman uglier, or filthier or more stinking' (cf. § 10).

    To him she spoke thus: 'I am thy bad actions, O youth of evil thoughts, of evil words, of evil deeds, of evil religion! It [pg 320] is on account of thy will and actions that I am hideous and vile, iniquitous and diseased, rotten and foul-smelling, unfortunate and distressed, as appears to thee (cf. §§ 11-12).

    'When thou sawest any one who performed the Yazishn and Drōn ceremonies, and praise and prayer and the service of God, and preserved and protected water and fire, cattle and trees, and other good creations, thou practisedst the will of Akharman and the demons, and improper actions. And when thou sawest one who provided hospitable reception, and gave something deservedly in gifts and charity, for the advantage of the good and worthy who came from far, and who were from near, thou wast avaricious, and shuttedst up thy door (cf. § 13).

    'And though I have been unholy (that is, I have been considered bad), I am made more unholy through thee; and though I have been frightful, I am made more frightful through thee; though I have been tremulous, I am made more tremulous through thee; though I am settled in the northern region of the demons, I am settled further north through thee; through these evil thoughts, through these evil words, and through these evil deeds, which thou practisedst. They curse me, a long time, in the long execration and evil communion of the Evil Spirit (cf. § 14).

    'Afterwards that soul of the wicked advanced the first footstep on Dūsh-hūmat (the place of evil thoughts), &c.' (The Book of Ardā Vīrāf, XVII, 12-27, as translated by Haug).

[^1346]: Cf. Yasna XXXI, 20: 'He who would deceive the holy One, to him afterwards (will be) a long weeping in the dark place, bad food and words of insult. O wicked! this is the place down which your own conscience will bring you through your own deeds.'

[^1347]: §§ 37-[38](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/errata.htm#4), 39-40, 41-42 are separate fragments.

[^1348]: One of the first disciples of Zoroaster; cf. Yt. XIII, 96.

[^1349]: Cf. [p. 33](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2306.htm#page_33), note [2](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2306.htm#fn_173).

[^1350]: § 38 = Yt. I, 31.

[^1351]: A Pahlavi translation of the following two fragments is found in MS. 33, Paris, Supplément Persan (edited in Études Iraniennes, II).

[^1352]: Cithra (Paris MS. p. 255).

[^1353]: 'How do they manifest their assistance?' (Pahl. tr. ibid.); that is to say, when do they assist their relations and countrymen? (see Yt. XIII, 49 seq.)

[^1354]: When men are instinct with good spirit and good thought.

[^1355]: The Pahlavi translation of this fragment has here §§ 14-16 of the Ātash Nyāyiś, then §§ 18-19 of Vendīdād XVIII. Therefore the whole passage is to be restored as follows:

    Ātar looks at the hands of all those who pass by: 'What does the friend bring to his friend . . . .?' (Ātash N. 14.)

    And if that passer-by brings him wood holily brought, or bundles of baresma holily tied up . . . ., then Ātar . . . . will bless him thus:

    May herds of oxen grow for thee . . . . (Ātash N. 15-16).

    In the first part of the night, Fire, the son of Ahura Mazda, calls the master of the house for help, saying:

    'Up! arise, thou master of the house . . . .' (Vend. XVIII, 18-19).

    'Then towards the dawning of the dawn . . . .' (see the text).

[^1356]: Cf. Vend. XVIII, 23.

[^1357]: 'He who has knowledge made,' or 'He who has the knowledge of what is made' (kartak dānishn); his other name Parōdarś is 'He who foresees.'

[^1358]: Here again a large passage is omitted: it can only partly be [pg 323] supplied from the Pahlavi translation; the words in brackets refer to Zend texts lost to us:

    'Then he flaps his wings and lifts up his voice, saying: "Arise, O men! \[and also women, grown-up people, and children, &c . . . . Put on well your girdle and shirt, wash your hands, put your girdle around your body, go and give food to the cattle and recite aloud the five holy Gāthas of Spitama Zarathuśtra."\]

    'Here the fiendish Būshyãsta . . . .' (see the text). Then the Pahlavi translation has: 'Never care for the three excellent things, good thoughts, good words, good deeds' (cf. Vend. XVIII, 25).

[pg 324]

### XXIII-XXIV. ĀFRĪN PAIGHAMBAR ZARTŪŚT AND VĪŚTĀSP YAŚT.

_'God taught the Zendávasta to Zartusht—a sublime work . . . . God said to Zartusht, "Go and before Sháh Gushtásp read this book, that he may come into the faith . . . . keep all my counsel and repeat it word by word to Sháh Gushtásp [^1359]." '_

_Zartusht, in obedience to God, went to the court of Gushtásp: 'He came forward and called down a blessing on the Shāh [^1360].' Then he read to him the Zandávasta and said: 'Learn its statutes and walk therein. If your desire is towards its laws, your abode shall be in the paradise of heaven. But if you turn away from its commandments, you shall bring down your crowned head to the dust. Your God will be displeased with you, and will overthrow your prosperous condition. At the last you shall descend into hell, if you hear not the counsel of the Almighty [^1361].'_

_These lines of the Zartusht-Namah are a summary of the following two Yaśts. The first, entitled 'The blessing of the prophet Zartūśt,' contains the words of blessing addressed by Zarathuśtra when appearing before the king. These words seem to have followed a similar blessing pronounced by Jāmāspa [^1362], the prime minister of Vīśtāspa [^1363]._

_Yaśt XXIV contains the exhortations of the prophet to the king to follow and closely adhere to the Law of Mazda. It is a counterpart to the XIXth Fargard of the Vendīdād, as Zarathuśtra plays here the same part to Vīśtāspa as Ahura does there to Zarathuśtra. It is, therefore, a summary of the Law, of the duties it_ [pg 325] _enforces and of the rewards it promises. This accounts for the strange disconnection apparent in it, which makes it a crux interpretum, as, besides the very corrupt state of the text, the chief difficulty of this Yaśt arises from the fact that many passages in it are incomplete quotations from the Vendīdād, or allusions to statements therein [^1364], which, when supplied, help a good deal to relieve this Yaśt from its apparent state of utter incoherence._

_For this translation I was able to avail myself of a Pahlavi translation, of which a copy was kindly lent to me by Mr. West. That translation is apparently of late date and often manifestly wrong; yet it was very useful to me in several passages, besides its giving a Zend text generally more correct and more correctly divided than the text in Westergaard's edition [^1365]._

_Yaśt XXIII was originally no independent Yaśt, being nothing more than the beginning of Yaśt XXIV, detached from it, with one slight alterations and inversions._

\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

## XXIII. ĀFRĪN PAIGHAMBAR ZARTŪŚT.

'I am a pious man, who speaks words of blessing.' {#XXIII:1}

—'Thou appearest unto me full of Glory.'

And Zarathuśtra spake unto king Vīśtāspa, saying: 'I bless thee, O man! O lord of the country! with the living of a good life, of an exalted life, of a long life. May thy men live long! May thy women live long! May sons be born unto thee of thy own body!

'Mayest thou have a son like Jāmāspa, and may he bless thee as (Jāmāspa blessed) Vīśtāspa (the lord) of the country [^1366]! {#XXIII:2}

[pg 326]

'Mayest thou be most beneficent, like Mazda!

'Mayest thou be fiend-smiting, like Thraētaona [^1367]!

'Mayest thou be strong, like Jāmāspa [^1368]!

'Mayest thou be well-armed, like Takhma-Urupa [^1369]!

'Mayest thou be glorious, like Yima Khshaēta, the good shepherd! {#XXIII:3}

'Mayest thou be instructed with a thousand senses, like Aži Dahāka, of the evil law [^1370]!

'Mayest thou be awful and most strong, like Keresāspa [^1371]!

'Mayest thou be a wise chief of assemblies, like Urvākhshaya [^1372]!

'Mayest thou be beautiful of body and without fault, like Syāvarshāna [^1373]!

'Mayest thou be rich in cattle, like an Āthwyanide [^1374]! {#XXIII:4}

'Mayest thou be rich in horses, like Pouruś-aspa [^1375]!

'Mayest thou be holy, like Zarathuśtra Spitama!

'Mayest thou be able to reach the Rangha, whose shores lie afar, as Vafra Navāza was [^1376]!

'Mayest thou be beloved by the gods and reverenced by men [^1377]!

[pg 327]

'May ten sons be born of you [^1378]! In three of them mayest thou be an Āthravan! In three of them mayest thou be a warrior! In three of them mayest thou be a tiller of the ground [^1379]! And may one be like thyself, O Vīśtāspa! {#XXIII:5}

'Mayest thou be swift-horsed, like the Sun [^1380]! {#XXIII:6}

'Mayest thou be resplendent, like the moon!

'Mayest thou be hot-burning, like fire!

'Mayest thou have piercing rays, like Mithra!

'Mayest thou be tall-formed and victorious, like the devout Sraosha [^1381]!

'Mayest thou follow a law of truth, like Rashnu [^1382]! {#XXIII:7}

'Mayest thou be a conqueror of thy foes, like Verethraghna [^1383], made by Ahura!

'Mayest thou have fulness of welfare, like Rāma Hvāstra [^1384]!

'Mayest thou be freed from sickness and death, like king Husravah [^1385]!

'Then the blessing goes for the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones [^1386]. {#XXIII:8}

'May it happen unto thee according to my blessing!

' [^1387] Let us embrace and propagate the good thoughts, good words, and good deeds that have been done and that will be done here and elsewhere, that we may be in the number of the good.

[pg 328]

_'Yathā ahū vairyō: The will of the Lord is the law of holiness . . . ._

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

_'\[Give\] unto that man brightness and glory, . . . . give him the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones.'_

[^1359]: The Zartusht-Namah, translated by E. B. Eastwick, in Wilson's Parsi Religion, p. 495.

[^1360]: Ibid. p. 499.

[^1361]: Ibid. p. 501.

[^1362]: See Yt. XXIII, 2; whether Anquetil's statement to that effect (Zend-Avesta II, 623) rests on independent tradition or only on the text of our Yaśt is not clear.

[^1363]: See above, [p. 70](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#page_70), note [1](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#fn_344).

[^1364]: For instance, §§ 28, 30, 31, 39, &c.

[^1365]: The various readings in Mr. West's manuscript are indicated by the letter W. in the notes.

[^1366]: See the introduction to this Yaśt and Yt. XXIV, 3, text and note.

[^1367]: Cf. Yt. V, 33.

[^1368]: Cf. Yt. V, 68

[^1369]: Cf. Yt. XV, 11.

[^1370]: Cf. Yt. V,29.

[^1371]: Cf. Yt. V, 37.

[^1372]: See Yt. XV, 28.

[^1373]: See [p. 64](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#page_64), note [1](http://www.sacred-texts.com/zor/sbe23/sbe2310.htm#fn_315).

[^1374]: One belonging to the Āthwya family, of which Thraētaona was a member. All of them bore names that show them to have been rich in cattle: Pūr-tōrā, Sōk-tōrā, Bōr-tōrā, &c. ('one with abundant oxen, with useful oxen, with the brown ox, &c.,' Bundahiś, tr. West, XXXI, 7, note 8).

[^1375]: Pouruś-aspa was the father of Zarathuśtra. His name means, 'He who possesses many horses,' πολύ-ιππος.

[^1376]: Cf. Yt. V, 61.

[^1377]: Cf. Yt. XXIV, 4.

[^1378]: Of Vīśtāspa and his wife Hutaosa.

[^1379]: Cf. Yt. XXIV, 4.

[^1380]: Cf. Sīrōzah, § 11.

[^1381]: Cf. Yt. XI.

[^1382]: Cf. Yt. XII, Introduction.

[^1383]: Cf. Yt. XIV.

[^1384]: Cf. Yt. XV.

[^1385]: Kai Khosrav went alive to Paradise (Firdausi).

[^1386]: He closes his blessing by wishing him bliss in heaven.

[^1387]: Yasna XXXV, 2 (4-5).

* * *

## XXIV. VĪŚTĀSP YAŚT.

#### I.

'I am a pious man, who speaks words of blessing,' thus said Zarathuśtra to the young king Vīśtāspa [^1388].—'She [^1389] appears to me full of Glory, O Zarathuśtra!'—'O young king Vīśtāspa! \[I bless thee [^1390]\] with the living of a good life, of an exalted life, of a long life. May thy men live long! May thy women live long! May sons be born unto thee of thy own body [^1391]! {#XXIV:1}

'Mayest thou thyself [^1392] be holy, like Zarathuśtra! {#XXIV:2}

'Mayest thou be rich in cattle, like an Āthwyanide [^1393]!

'Mayest thou be rich in horses, like Pouruś-aspa [^1394]!

'Mayest thou have a good share of bliss [^1395], like king Husravah!

'Mayest thou have strength to reach the Rangha, whose way lies afar, as Vafra Navāza did [^1396].

[pg 329]

'May ten sons be born of thy own body [^1397]! three as Āthravans [^1398], three as warriors [^1399], three as tillers of the ground [^1400]! May one of them be like Jāmāspa [^1401], that he may bless thee with great and ever greater happiness [^1402]! {#XXIV:3}

'Mayest thou be freed from sickness and death, like Peshō-tanu [^1403]. {#XXIV:4}

'Mayest thou have piercing rays, like Mithra!

'Mayest thou be warm, like the moon!

'Mayest thou be [^1404] resplendent, like fire!

'Mayest thou be long-lived, as long-lived as an old man can be [^1405]!

'And when thou hast fulfilled a duration of a thousand years, \[mayest thou obtain\] the bright, all-happy, blissful abode of the holy Ones! {#XXIV:5}

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

[pg 330]

#### II.

 [^1406]. 'Give [^1407] him strength and victory! Give him welfare in cattle and bread [^1408]!' thus said Zarathuśtra to the young king Vīśtāspa! 'Give him a great number [^1409] of male children, praisers [^1410] \[of God\] and chiefs in assemblies, who smite and are not smitten, who smite at one stroke their enemies, who smite at one stroke their foes, ever in joy and ready to help. {#XXIV:6}

'Ye gods of full Glory, ye gods of full healing, let your greatness become manifest!' {#XXIV:7}

Zarathuśtra addressed him, saying: 'O young king Vīśtāspa! May their greatness become manifest as it is called for! {#XXIV:8}

'Ye Waters, impart and give your Glory to the man who offers you a sacrifice!

'This is the boon we beg (for thee) of Ashi Vanguhi [^1411], of Rāta [^1412], with eyes of love.'

Pāreṇdi [^1413], of the light chariot, follows: 'Mayest thou [^1414] become manifest unto him, the young king Vīśtāspa! {#XXIV:9}

'May plenty dwell in this house, standing upon high columns and rich in food [^1415]! Thou wilt never [pg 331] offer and give bad food to a priest: for a priest must be to thee like the brightest [^1416] offspring of thy own blood.'

Zarathuśtra spake unto him: 'O young king Vīśtāspa! {#XXIV:10}

'He who supports the Law of the worshippers of Mazda, as a brother or as a friend, he who treats her friendly in any way, looks to keep off want of food from her [^1417].'

The holy Zarathuśtra preached that law to Frashaośtra [^1418] and Jāmāspa: 'May ye practise holiness and thrive, O young Frashaośtra (and Jāmāspa)!' {#XXIV:11}

Thus said Ahura Mazda unto the holy Zarathuśtra, and thus again did Zarathuśtra say unto the young king Vīśtāspa: 'Have no bad priests or unfriendly priests; for bad priests or unfriendly priests will bring about much harm, and, though thou wish to sacrifice, it will be to the Amesha-Speṇtas as if no sacrifice had been offered [^1419]. {#XXIV:12}

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### III.

'When I teach thee, that thou mayest do the same to thy son [^1420], O Vīśtāspa! receive thou well that teaching; that will make thee rich in children and rich in milk; rich in seed, in fat, in milk [^1421]. {#XXIV:13}

[pg 332]

'Thus do we announce unto thee, Ahura Mazda, and Sraosha, and Ashi, and the Law of the worshippers of Mazda, with the whole of all her hymns, with the whole of all her deeds, with the whole of her performances; the Law of Mazda, who obtains her wishes, who makes the world grow, who listens to the songs and rejoices the faithful man at his wish; who protects the faithful man, who maintains the faithful man; {#XXIV:14}

'From whom come the knowledge of holiness and the increase in holiness of the world of the holy Principle, and without whom [^1422] no faithful man [^1423] can know holiness. {#XXIV:15}

'To thee [^1424] come every Hāvanan, every Ātare-vakhsha, every Frabaretar, every Ābereṭ, every Āsnātar, every Rathwiśkar, every Sraoshā-varez [^1425];

'Every priest, every warrior, every husbandman; every master of a house, every lord of a borough, every lord of a town, every lord of a province; {#XXIV:16}

'Every youth of good thoughts, good words, good deeds, and good religion; every youth who speaks the right words; every one who performs the next-of-kin marriage [^1426]; every itinerant priest; every mistress of a house; every wandering priest, obedient to the Law. {#XXIV:17}

'To thee come all the performers [^1427] (of holiness), all the masters of holiness, who, to the [pg 333] number of three and thirty [^1428], stand next to Hāvani, being masters of holiness. {#XXIV:18}

'May they be fully protected [^1429] in thee, O young king Vīśtāspa! While thou smitest thy adversaries, thy foes, those who hate thee, a hundred times a hundred for a hundred [^1430], a thousand times a thousand for a thousand, ten thousand times ten thousand for ten thousand, myriads of myriads for a myriad. {#XXIV:19}

'Proclaim thou that word, as we did proclaim it unto thee! {#XXIV:20}

'O Maker of the good world! Ahura Mazda, I worship thee with a sacrifice, I worship and forward thee with a sacrifice, I worship this creation of Ahura Mazda.'

 [^1431]. The young king Vīśtāspa asked Zarathuśtra: 'With what manner of sacrifice shall I worship, with what manner of sacrifice shall I worship and forward this creation of Ahura Mazda?' {#XXIV:21}

Zarathuśtra answered: 'We will make it known unto thee, O young king Vīśtāspa! {#XXIV:22}

'Go towards that tree that is beautiful, high-growing, and mighty amongst the high-growing trees, and say thou these words: "Hail to thee! O good, holy tree, made by Mazda! Ashem Vohū!"

'Let the faithful man cut off twigs of baresma, either one, or two, or three: let him bind them and [pg 334] tie them up according to the rites, being bound and unbound according to the rites. {#XXIV:23}

'The smallest twig of Haoma, pounded according to the rules, the smallest twig prepared for sacrifice, gives royalty to the man (who does it).'

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### IV.

 [^1432]. Zarathuśtra said: 'O young king Vīśtāspa! {#XXIV:24}

'Invoke Ahura Mazda, who is full of Glory, Ahura Mazda, and the sovereign Heaven, the boundless Time, and Vayu who works highly.

'Invoke the powerful Wind, made by Mazda, and Fate. {#XXIV:25}

'Repeat thou those words, that the god invoked may give thee the boon wished for; that thou, strong, and belonging to the creation of the good Spirit, mayest smite and take away the Druj and watch with full success those who hate thee; smite down thy foes, and destroy at one stroke thy adversaries, thy enemies, and those who hate thee [^1433].

'Proclaim thou those prayers: they will cleanse thy body from deeds of lust [^1434], O young king Vīśtāspa! {#XXIV:26}

'I will worship thee, O Fire, son of Ahura Mazda, who art a valiant warrior. He falls upon the fiend Kuṇda [^1435], who is drunken without drinking, upon the men of the Druj, the slothful ones [^1436], the wicked Daēva-worshippers, who live in sin.

[pg 335]

'He [^1437] trembles at the way [^1438] made by Time and open both to the wicked and to the righteous. {#XXIV:27}

'They [^1439] tremble at the perfume of his soul [^1440], as a sheep does on which a wolf is falling.

'Reciting the whole collection of the Staota Yēsnya [^1441] prayers brings one up all the way to the blessed Garō-nmāna, the palace beautifully made. That indeed is the way. {#XXIV:28}

'That man does not follow the way of the Law, O Zarathuśtra [^1442]! who commits the Baodhō-(varśta) crime [^1443] with a damsel and an old woman [^1444],' said Zarathuśtra to the young king Vīśtāspa. {#XXIV:29}

'Let him [^1445] praise the Law, O Spitama Zarathuśtra! and long for it and embrace the whole of the Law, as an excellent horse turns back from the wrong way and goes along the right one, smiting the many Drujes [^1446].

'Go forward with praises, go forward the way of the good Mazdean law and of all those who walk in her ways, men and women. {#XXIV:30}

[pg 336]

'He who wishes to seize the heavenly reward [^1447], will seize it by giving gifts to him who holds up (the Law) to us [^1448] in this world here below [^1449] . . .

'Let him [^1450] give (the Law) to him who is unfriendly to her, that he may become friendly. {#XXIV:31}

'Wash thy hands with water, not with gōmēz [^1451], and let thy son, who will be born of thy wife [^1452], do the same.

'Thus thy thought will be powerful to smite him [^1453], who is not so [^1454]; thy speech will be powerful to smite him, who is not so; thy deed will be powerful to smite him.

' "Hear me! Forgive me [^1455]!"—We, the Amesha-Speṇtas, will come and show thee, O Zarathuśtra! the way to that world [^1456], to long glory in the spiritual world, to long happiness of the soul in Paradise; {#XXIV:32}

'To bliss and Paradise, to the Garō-nmāna of Ahura Mazda, beautifully made and fully adorned, [pg 337] when his soul goes out of his body through the will of fate, when I, Ahura Mazda, when I, Ahura Mazda, gently show him his way as he asks for it. {#XXIV:33}

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### V.

'They [^1457] will impart to thee full brightness and Glory. {#XXIV:34}

'They will give him [^1458] quick [^1459] and swift horses, and good sons.

'He wishes to go to the Law, the young king Vīśtāspa.'

Zarathuśtra said: 'Let him who is unfriendly to her become a follower of the Law of Mazda, such as we proclaim it.

'Proclaim thou ever (unto the poor): "Ever mayest thou wait here for the refuse that is brought unto thee, brought by those who have profusion of wealth [^1460]!" Thus the Druj will not fall upon thee and throw thee away; thou wilt wield kingly power there [^1461]. {#XXIV:35}

'The Law of Mazda will not deliver thee unto pain [^1462]. Thou art entreated (for charity) by the whole of the living world, and she [^1463] is ever standing at thy door in the person of thy brethren in the faith: beggars are ever standing at the door of the stranger, amongst those who beg for bread. {#XXIV:36}

[pg 338]

'Ever will that bread be burning coal upon thy head [^1464].

'The good, holy Rāta [^1465], made by Mazda, goes and nurses thy bright offspring [^1466].'

Zarathuśtra addressed Vīśtāspa, saying: 'O young king Vīśtāspa! The Law of Mazda, O my son! will give thy offspring the victorious strength that destroys the fiends. {#XXIV:37}

'Let no thought of Angra Mainyu ever infect thee, so that thou shouldst indulge in evil lusts, make derision and idolatry, and shut (to the poor) the door of thy house [^1467].

 [^1468]. 'Ātar thus blesses the man who brings incense to him, being pleased with him and not angry, and fed as he required: "May herds of oxen grow for thee, and increase of sons! May fate and its decrees bring thee the boons thou wishest for! Therefore do thou invoke and praise (me) excellently in this glorious world! That I may have unceasing food, full of the glory of Mazda [^1469] and with which I am well pleased." {#XXIV:38}

'O Mazda! take for thyself the words of our praise: of these words I speak and speak again, the strength and victorious vigour, the power of health and healing, the fulness, increase, and growth. {#XXIV:39}

'Bring it together with the words of hymns up to the Garō-nmāna of Ahura Mazda. He will [^1470] first [pg 339] enter there. Therefore do thou pronounce these prayers.

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### VI.

'Converse ye with the Amesha-Speṇtas,' said Zarathuśtra unto the young king Vīśtāspa, and with the devout Sraosha, and Nairyō-sangha, the tall-formed, and Ātar, the son of Ahura Mazda, and the well-desired kingly Glory. {#XXIV:40}

'Men with lustful deeds address the body [^1471]; but thou, all the night long, address the heavenly Wisdom [^1472]; but thou, all night long, call for the Wisdom that will keep thee awake. {#XXIV:41}

'Three times a day raise thyself up and go to take care of the beneficent cattle.

'Of these men may the lordship [^1473] belong to the wisest of all beings, O Zarathuśtra! May their lord belong to the wisest, O Zarathuśtra! Let him show them the way of holiness, let him show them at once the way thereto, which the Law of the worshippers of Mazda enters victoriously. Thus the soul of man, in the joy of perfect holiness, walks over the bridge, known afar, the powerful Cinvaṭ-bridge [^1474], the well-kept, and kept by virtue. {#XXIV:42}

'How the worlds were arranged was said to thee first, O Zarathuśtra! Zarathuśtra said it again to the young king Vīśtāspa; therefore do thou [^1475] praise him [^1476] who keeps and maintains the moon and the sun. {#XXIV:43}

[pg 340]

'He who has little friendship for the Law, I have placed him down below to suffer.'

Thus said Angra Mainyu, he who has no Glory in him, who is full of death: 'This is an unbeliever, let us throw him down below; this is a liar, or a traitor to his relatives, and like a mad dog who wounds cattle and men; but the dog who inflicts wounds pays for it as for wilful murder [^1477]. {#XXIV:44}

'The first time he shall smite a faithful man, the first time he shall wound a faithful man, he shall pay for it as for wilful murder.

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### VII.

'Mayest thou receive [^1478], O holy young king Vīśtāspa! (a house) with a hundred . . . . [^1479], ten thousand large windows, ten thousand small windows, all the year long [^1480], O holy Vīśtāspa! never growing old, never dying, never decaying, never rotting, giving plenty of meat, plenty of food, plenty of clothes to the other worshippers of Mazda. {#XXIV:45}

'May all boons be bestowed upon thee, as I proclaim it unto thee! May the Amesha-Speṇtas impart to thee their brightness and glory and plenty [^1481]! May they give him quick and swift horses and good sons, strong, great in all things, powerful to sing the hymns. {#XXIV:46}

[pg 341]

'He wields his power according to the wish of Ahura Mazda, the Good Spirit, and for the destruction of the Evil Spirit, whichever of two men goes quicker to perform a sacrifice (to Ahura); but if he chooses to perform the sacrifice and prayer to us not in the right way, he does not wield the right power, he will not reign [^1482]. {#XXIV:47}

'He will receive bad treatment in the next world, though he has been the sovereign of a country, with good horses to ride and good chariots to drive. Give royalty to that man, O Zarathuśtra! who gives royalty unto thee with good will [^1483]. {#XXIV:48}

 [^1484]. 'Thou shalt keep away the evil by this holy spell: "Of thee \[O child!\] I will cleanse the birth and growth; of thee \[O woman!\] I will make the body and the strength pure; I make thee a woman rich in children and rich in milk; a woman rich in seed, in milk, and in offspring. For thee I shall make springs run and flow towards the pastures that will give food to the child." {#XXIV:49}

'Do not deliver me [^1485] into the hands of the fiend [^1486]; if the fiend take hold of me, then fever with loss of all joy will dry up the milk of the good Speṇta-Ārmaiti [^1487]. The fiend is powerful to distress, and to dry up the milk of the woman who indulges in lust and of all females. {#XXIV:50}

'The perfume of fire, pleasant to the Maker, [pg 342] Ahura Mazda, takes them [^1488] away from afar; . . . . [^1489]; and all those that harm the creation of the Good Spirit are destroyed [^1490]; {#XXIV:51}

'Whom Mithra, and Rashnu Raziśta, and the Law of the worshippers of Mazda wish to be taken far away, longing for a man who is eager to perform and does perform the ceremonies he has been taught; . . . [^1491] {#XXIV:52}

_'Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

#### VIII [^1492].

'The words of the Vahiśtōiśti [^1493] Gātha are to be sung: "Happy is he, O holy Vīśtāspa! happy the man, whoever he be, to whom Ahura Mazda gives the full accomplishment of his wishes." {#XXIV:53}

'Where does his soul abide on that night [^1494]?'

Ahura Mazda answered: 'O my son, Frashaośtra! It takes its seat near the head, singing the Uśtavaiti Gātha and proclaiming happiness: "Happy is he, happy the man whoever he be!" {#XXIV:54}

'On the first night, his soul sits in Good Words [^1495]; [pg 343] on the second night, it sits in Good Deeds; on the third night, it goes along the ways (to Garō-nmāna).

'At the end of the third night, O my son, Frashaośtra! when the dawn appears, it seems to the soul of the faithful one as if it were brought amidst plants \[and scents: it seems as if a wind were blowing from the region of the south, from the regions of the south\] [^1496], a sweet-scented wind, sweeter-scented than any other wind in the world, and it seems to his soul as if he were inhaling that wind with the nose, and it asks, saying: "Whence does that wind blow, the sweetest-scented wind I ever inhaled with my nose?" {#XXIV:55}

'And it seems to him as if his own conscience were advancing to him in that wind, in the shape of a maiden fair, bright, white-armed, strong, tall-formed, high-standing, thick-breasted, beautiful of body, noble, of a glorious seed, of the size of a maid in her fifteenth year, as fair as the fairest things in the world. {#XXIV:56}

'And the soul of the faithful one addressed her, asking: "What maid art thou, who art the fairest maid I have ever seen?" {#XXIV:57}

'And she, being his own conscience, answers him: "O thou youth, of good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, of good religion! I am thy own conscience. {#XXIV:58}

' "Everybody did love thee for that greatness, goodness, fairness, sweet-scentedness, victorious strength, and freedom from sorrow, in which thou [pg 344] dost appear to me; \[and so thou, O youth of good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, of good religion! didst love me for that greatness, goodness, fairness, sweet-scentedness, victorious strength, and freedom from sorrow, in which I appear to thee.

' "When thou wouldst see a man [^1497]\] making derision and deeds of idolatry, or rejecting (the poor) and shutting (his door), then, thou wouldst sit, singing the Gāthas, and worshipping the good waters, and Ātar, the son of Ahura Mazda, and rejoicing the faithful that would come from near or from afar. {#XXIV:59}

' "I was lovely, and thou madest me still lovelier; I was fair, and thou madest me still fairer; I was desirable, and thou madest me still more desirable; I was sitting in a forward place, and thou madest me sit in the foremost place, through this good thought, through this good speech, through this good deed of thine; and so henceforth men worship me for my having long sacrificed unto and conversed with Ahura Mazda." {#XXIV:60}

'The first step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Thought Paradise; the second step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Word Paradise; the third step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Good-Deed Paradise; the fourth step that the soul of the faithful man made, placed him in the Endless Light. {#XXIV:61}

'Then one of the faithful, who had departed before him, asked, saying: "How didst thou depart this life, thou holy man? How didst thou come, [pg 345] thou holy man! from the abodes full of cattle and full of the wishes and enjoyments of love? from the material world into the world of the spirit? from the decaying world into the undecaying one? How long did thy felicity last?" ' {#XXIV:62}

And Ahura Mazda answered: 'Ask him not what thou askest him, who has just gone the dreary way, full of fear and distress, when the body and the soul part from one another. {#XXIV:63}

'\[Let him eat\] of the food brought to him, of the oil of Zaremaya: this is the food for the youth of good thoughts, of good words, of good deeds, of good religion, after he has departed this life; this is the food for the holy woman, rich in good thoughts, good words, and good deeds, well-principled, and obedient to her husband, after she has departed this life.' {#XXIV:64}

Spitama Zarathuśtra said to the young king Vīśtāspa: 'To what land shall I turn, O Ahura Mazda? To whom shall I go with praying [^1498]? {#XXIV:65}

_Ashem Vohū: Holiness is the best of all good . . . ._

I cannot make anything of these words, nor reconcile them with the Pahlavi translation: 'It is not fair when he wishes weal for his own person; that is to say, when, being satisfied himself, he does not satisfy other people and wishes comfort for himself. (Make the Law of Mazda current, till the time when) the victorious Sōshyōsh will make it current.' The last three Zend words appear to be abridged from a longer passage.
